  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_974d610f-9dbd-4212-bf1c-7597b57d9210'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText8020575065498862639" style="display:none">In case you’re wondering, this is not a love story.<br /><br />My name is Tori Spring. I like to sleep and I like to blog. Last year – before all that stuff with Charlie and before I had to face the harsh realities of A-Levels and university applications and the fact that one day I really will have to start talking to people – I had friends. Things were very different, I guess, but that’s all over now.<br /><br />Now there’s Solitaire. And Michael Holden.<br /><br />I don’t know what Solitaire are trying to do, and I don’t care about Michael Holden.<br />I really don’t.<br /><br />This incredible debut novel by outstanding young author Alice Oseman is perfect for fans of John Green, Rainbow Rowell and all unflinchingly honest writers.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062335685" href="/book/show/22588585-solitaire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=underrated">underrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1244998000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9252066625663662249"><i>“But books–they’re different. When you watch a film, you’re sort of an outsider looking in. With a book–you’re right there. You are inside. You are the main character.”</i><br/><br/>4.5/5 stars<br/><br/>I first heard about <i>Solitaire</i> on Tumblr. I've been following Alice Oseman ever since and I desperately wanted to read her novel. So when I finally, finally! found it at the library I think I maybe made some loud joyful sound and hugged it...yeah.<br/><br/>I loved <i>Solitaire</i> from the beginning. I couldn't wait to read about all the</span>
  <span id="freeText9252066625663662249" style="display:none"><i>“But books–they’re different. When you watch a film, you’re sort of an outsider looking in. With a book–you’re right there. You are inside. You are the main character.”</i><br /><br />4.5/5 stars<br /><br />I first heard about <i>Solitaire</i> on Tumblr. I've been following Alice Oseman ever since and I desperately wanted to read her novel. So when I finally, finally! found it at the library I think I maybe made some loud joyful sound and hugged it...yeah.<br /><br />I loved <i>Solitaire</i> from the beginning. I couldn't wait to read about all the characters I had already heard of and I instantly fell in love with Nick&amp;Charlie.<br />Solitaire is, in general, an extremely relatable YA novel. It deals with all the stuff our generation deals with, especially anxiety, depression and lgbt+ topics. It makes me very happy to see all this put into words and represented in this wonderful story.<br /><br />Although I disliked a few characters - I did not really understand why the main character even put up with them - and did expect something else from the ending, I just have to give 5 stars. I believe this is a book you either love or hate, understand or don't. And I love and understand.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_1789705821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1789705821" />
    <a title="Romie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33510193-romie"><img alt="Romie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579037929p2/33510193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1789705821?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Romie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Romie" href="/user/show/33510193-romie">Romie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007559220" href="/book/show/40683413-solitaire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=disabilities-mental-health">disabilities-mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=nearly-a-favourite">nearly-a-favourite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33510193-romie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1789705821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1469139472450580333"><i>Just because someone smiles doesn’t mean that they’re happy.</i><br/><br/>This isn’t a book about happy people. I don’t even think this book was made for happy people, they would dislike it, say everything inside this book is utter bullshit. But it isn’t. It’s the absolute truth.<br/><br/>This book broke me, I think I’m reading it at the exact right moment in my life. 16-year-old me wouldn’t have liked it all that much, she would have sympathised with the characters, but she wouldn’t have understood them like 21-year-o</span>
  <span id="freeText1469139472450580333" style="display:none"><i>Just because someone smiles doesn’t mean that they’re happy.</i><br /><br />This isn’t a book about happy people. I don’t even think this book was made for happy people, they would dislike it, say everything inside this book is utter bullshit. But it isn’t. It’s the absolute truth.<br /><br />This book broke me, I think I’m reading it at the exact right moment in my life. 16-year-old me wouldn’t have liked it all that much, she would have sympathised with the characters, but she wouldn’t have understood them like 21-year-old me did.<br /><br />This is the story of sad &amp; introvert Tori Spring. Nothing about being sad or introvert is wrong. That’s just the way she is. And yet people judge her for being like this. This say she doesn’t try enough to make friends, or to care about anything, and maybe it’s true, it probably is, but they’re not her. They don’t understand what’s going on inside her head. They don’t know how much she actually cares about her brother Charlie, the best person in the entire world, or how the things that happened to him broke her because he’s her little brother and nothing bad should happen to him. They don’t know that she’s sad 95% of the time but can do nothing about it because this isn’t just her deciding to be sad, this is her experiencing her life. Tori Spring was born in a world in which you should smile all the time and answer ‘I’m fine’ to every ‘How are you?’ Tori Spring was born into an extrovert and fake happy world, but why should she bend to the world’s will and be like that as well? This isn’t her.<br /><br />One day she meets angry boy Michael Holden. Angry at the world for expecting him to be someone he’s not. Angry at people for thinking him weird and not worthy of their attention and respect when he’s just being himself. Angry all the time. But hiding it. Hiding it because people would judge him even more, they would make him feel even more lonely than he is now. Michael Holden is the softest boy you will ever meet. He’s angry but that doesn’t he isn’t trying to make Tori happy, really happy, not fake. He’s not trying to save her, she doesn’t need to be saved, she needs to see she’s not alone in this world, that people like her exist. Michael Holden doesn’t want to save her, and he doesn’t need to be saved either. They just both need someone to help them. And their this person for each other.<br /><br />Ultimately this is a book about family and friendship. The family dynamic between the Spring siblings is one of the best I’ve read about. They’re a bunch of precious human beings who deserve for good things to happen to them. They’re trying to make their way through this world the best way they can, sometimes they fail, but they got each other to help them get up when they fall.<br /><br />This book isn’t perfect, but it was perfectly real, and I needed it.<br /><br /><i>There comes a point, though, when you can’t keep looking after other people any more. You have to start looking after yourself.</i><br /><br />4.75</span>
  <a data-text-id="1469139472450580333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1269036067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1269036067" />
    <a title="Lea (drumsofautumn)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7285286-lea-drumsofautumn"><img alt="Lea (drumsofautumn)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592339546p2/7285286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1269036067?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lea (drumsofautumn)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lea (drumsofautumn)" href="/user/show/7285286-lea-drumsofautumn">Lea (drumsofautumn)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1269036067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12792228273079959502">I really wanted to write a very detailed, slightly objective review of this but honestly I'm realizing I just can't. <b>I thought this book was super problematic</b> so I'm just gonna word vomit.<br/>FIRST OF ALL big ass trigger warnings for suicide/suicidal thoughts, self-harm and eating disorders. Pretty sure there's more so please be very aware and feel free to ask me if you want to know about any specific ones!<br/><br/>I know the main character is relatable for many and I hope that any of you who read this will </span>
  <span id="freeText12792228273079959502" style="display:none">I really wanted to write a very detailed, slightly objective review of this but honestly I'm realizing I just can't. <b>I thought this book was super problematic</b> so I'm just gonna word vomit.<br />FIRST OF ALL big ass trigger warnings for suicide/suicidal thoughts, self-harm and eating disorders. Pretty sure there's more so please be very aware and feel free to ask me if you want to know about any specific ones!<br /><br />I know the main character is relatable for many and I hope that any of you who read this will understand that anything I say in this is <b>nothing against your or your experiences</b>. This is a very personal opinion based on MY personal experiences but also based on the fact that I am much older than the main character. All I know is that I think this book is incredibly harmful.<br /><br />Let's talk about Tori's brother a little bit first because that is what I found most disturbing. I think I could have been okay with lots of things in this book but this pointed out how problematic it truly is.<br />Charlie tries to kill himself, he is self-harming and has an eating disorder. And what happens after he gets out of the hospital after that first suicide attempt? I GUESS NOTHING! <b>Not once is therapy even mentioned</b> except for a little bit of treatment when Charlie is in the hospital. I mean please DO feel free to correct me on this but I don't think it was ever mentioned that Charlie is or WAS in therapy. Say what you want about the way mental health and illness is portrayed in this book in general but it is NOT okay to basically ignore a suicide attempt! Tori even mentions that she sees Charlie wearing long-sleeved shirts quite a lot AND I GUESS NOBODY IS FUCKING BOTHERED BY A SUICIDAL, SELF-HARMING PERSON WEARING LONG SLEEVES ALL THE TIME? I don't know man.. AM I OVER-ANALYZING THIS???? It's just really fucking problematic to me.<br /><br />Okay so, about Tori. Completely separate to what is actually going on with her mental health, I found super problematic is that apparently Tori was the one who found her brother bleeding in the bathtub after that first suicide attempt. And I guess nobody ever cared about that either? Oh, she just saw her brother bleeding to death, that's fine, A SIXTEEN YEAR OLD GIRL CAN HANDLE IT!!!! WHAT!!!!!!!!!!!!!!<br /><br />Also I hated the portrayal of Tori's parents. I get it, it's supposed to be that way but I just added to the overall problematic shit that this book had. How can the father of a suicidal son not be worried when he gets into his daughter's room after she spend the whole day in bed? How is his only commentary "Oh, that's just teenagers, am I right?" How is NOT EVERY SINGLE ALARM SIGNAL IN HIS HEAD GOING OFF? Yeah, that would be dramatic and annoying of him but it's how a parent should react. Of course there's shitty parents out there that wouldn't react that way. But <b>NOBODY in this book ever really cares</b> - so couldn't we at least have one parent be a little bit less problematic?<br /><br />There's also a bunch of super graphic descriptions of how Tori just wants everybody around her to die and it was just too much. I get it, sometimes you're like <i>I hate everybody, please die</i> but it's more like "I would pick up a gun and shoot everybody in the head and I would see them bleed to death." I honestly didn't really understand why this needed to be so graphic?<br /><br />And why the fuck is the tagline "this is not a love story"? <b>IT IS a love story!</b> And that is perfectly fine but not if you try to sell it like it's not, like a romantic storyline should be something to look down on. Honestly the love story was almost one of my favourite parts. I liked the basic romantic storyline, I even liked the love interest and I wanted them to get together. <br /><br />BUT I thought <b>there was also a little bit of the "love can heal you" trope.</b><br />Tori never ever smiles. She doesn't find joy in anything. She hates everything. But when she talks to Michael she smiles.<br />Tori spends her whole day in bed and doesn't want to talk to anybody. She find out Michael has an important event where he needs support. She jumps out of bed and goes to that event.<br />SO??? I DON'T REALLY GET IT???? Is this supposed to be a portrayal of a teenager just being a little bit sad and kind of stuck in a weird place and then she finally finds someone who cares about her and so things get better for her? Because that would be a legit thing for me. I'd be fine with that as long as it's made clear.<br />But it's never really mentioned. We never really know if Tori has depression or what the fuck is even going on. So from everything we read - it does seem Tori is <i>supposed to be</i> a character with depression. And it's basically the most cliche portrayal of depression ever and it's just upsetting - especially when THEN a love interest can swoop in and make things better.<br /><br />So - as you can tell, I really didn't like this book. After writing this review I'm even thinking of giving it only a 1 star rating but there were certain aspects that I enjoyed. It was just that with everything I have experienced it was an incredibly upsetting read for me.<br />I did think of DNFing it but I thought maybe there'd be a redemption arc or something. There simply wasn't. So I'm left with this horrible feeling and <b>I just don't think this book is a good representation for mental health.</b> It's harmful and problematic and I really wouldn't recommend it.<br /><br />♦ <a href="https://www.youtube.com/drumsofautumn" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Booktube Channel</a> ♦ <a href="https://twitter.com/drumsofautumn" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ♦ <a href="https://instagram.com/drumsofautumn" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ♦</span>
  <a data-text-id="12792228273079959502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2161581293" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2161581293" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2161581293?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2161581293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1116762605058730520"><b>I think this is one of those books you either love or hate</b> the reviews seem very polarising - I'm not sure exactly where I sit yet. I know I did enjoy it overall, mostly because of the writing style. I love Alice Oseman's writing, it flows so well you just get so caught up in it and I think she writes teenagers incredibly well. <br/><br/>I didn't love this anywhere near as close as I loved Radio Silence, but also this is Alice's debut, and I think it's nice to see how much she's grown and improved. <br/><br/>I know</span>
  <span id="freeText1116762605058730520" style="display:none"><b>I think this is one of those books you either love or hate</b> the reviews seem very polarising - I'm not sure exactly where I sit yet. I know I did enjoy it overall, mostly because of the writing style. I love Alice Oseman's writing, it flows so well you just get so caught up in it and I think she writes teenagers incredibly well. <br /><br />I didn't love this anywhere near as close as I loved Radio Silence, but also this is Alice's debut, and I think it's nice to see how much she's grown and improved. <br /><br />I know I loved Nick and Charlie, but I already loved them before this book thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34235800.Heartstopper" title="Heartstopper by Alice Oseman" rel="nofollow noopener">Heartstopper</a> so I don't know if it counts as a positive to be accredited to this book. I also think Tori was an interesting narrator - maybe she's not <i>likeable</i>, but I don't think every 16 year old is. I don't think every character needs to be, either. I think teenagers definitely can be jaded and cynical and pessimistic, and I think it's something you kinda grow out of. I think I can relate to Tori at age 16, I hope I'm not as much like that anymore. But I enjoyed the perspective, even if it wasn't likeable, it was honest and authentically teen. <br /><br />I think overall, I'm not sure if I feel like I love how the issues were dealt with, and I don't know if I <u>get</u> this book. <br /><br />So I'm not gonna rate this yet? I kinda want to take a day or so to think about it overall. All I know for sure is I definitely don't feel the immediate connection to this book I felt to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25322449.Radio_Silence" title="Radio Silence by Alice Oseman" rel="nofollow noopener">Radio Silence</a></span>

<div id="review_2989674743" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2989674743" />
    <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze"><img alt="Emer (A Little Haze)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390599p2/4629647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2989674743?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/40377575-solitaire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2019">read2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=1star">1star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2989674743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4262783107762805812">Lol no. <br/><br/>This book has such inflated notions of itself but the execution is abysmal. <br/><br/>The MC Tori is supposed to be this sad and chronically depressed person that as a reader we are supposed to empathise with... But instead she's just a judgmental jerk! Honestly there's a difference between writing legitimate anxiety and depression versus general teenage malaise at life... <br/>And sadly this book got both things wrong. *smh Solitaire* <br/>Look I get what the aims were, but Oseman did not craft her MC well</span>
  <span id="freeText4262783107762805812" style="display:none">Lol no. <br /><br />This book has such inflated notions of itself but the execution is abysmal. <br /><br />The MC Tori is supposed to be this sad and chronically depressed person that as a reader we are supposed to empathise with... But instead she's just a judgmental jerk! Honestly there's a difference between writing legitimate anxiety and depression versus general teenage malaise at life... <br />And sadly this book got both things wrong. *smh Solitaire* <br />Look I get what the aims were, but Oseman did not craft her MC well enough to actually truly convey the nuance of depression and of being introverted. The idea was great... Execution poor. <br /><br />And for the tag line to say this is not a love story... ONLY FOR IT TO BE A LOVE STORY!!!<br />I cry laughing. <br />Like get over yourself already book. There's nothing wrong with writing about love. Stop trying to shame the greatest of human emotions.<br /><br />I've just discovered that Solitaire was written by Alice Oseman when she was a teenager and it makes perfect sense. Because this feels so juvenile which is both sad and annoying because think of freaking Frankenstein written by an adolescent Mary Shelley and how deliciously layered that book is. This immature drivel-fest just reinforces negative teenage stereotypes and my inner fifteen year old is not happy with that. TEENAGERS ARE BETTER THAN THIS RIDICULOUS BOOK!!!! <br /><br />Anyway there's so much in this that irked me...<br />The unexplained hostility for Tori's parents... Omg there's this scene where Tori basically concludes that her mother loathes Tori with every fibre of her being because... Wait for it... HER MOTHER REFUSES TO IRON HER SCHOOL UNIFORM... I mean right??? <br />Terrible mothering definitely... <br />Like social services need to get on that for sure.....<br />OMG TORI YOU ARE 17 YEARS OLD SO YOU CAN IRON YOUR OWN GOD DAMNED CLOTHES YOU USELESS ENTITLED TOSSER!!! I mean your poor mother has enough to be dealing with that she can't suddenly just drop everything to iron your school skirt. <br /><br />Gosh there were so many eye roll moments in this. <br /><br />Wtf was that handling of her brother's eating disorder and self harming storyline??? First up this book needs MASSIVE content and trigger warnings for both. Plus suicidal ideation. When will books come with content warnings as standard????? <br />But yes, the actual handling of all these topics was so sub-par. It felt quite sensationalist to me rather than carefully exploring these mental health issues. This book was just too chock full of bland characters with *problems*. If perhaps Oseman had picked one of these mental health issues and properly researched and explained it then this book could very much have been a truly interesting exploration into teenage depression. <br /><br />Also lol at the book trying to compare itself to The Catcher in the Rye in the closing stages... Solitaire freaking wishes it had the quality of prose, the delicate pacing of the narrative and the true authentic nature of Holden from Catcher. <br /><br />I really didn't like this book at all. <br />The prose felt awkward. <br />The characters barely more than pastiches. <br />The mysterious identity of Solitaire laughably obvious.<br />And the climax just plain ridiculous. <br /><br />I borrowed this from the library but I own both Radio Silence and I Was Born For This that are also written by Alice Oseman. In addition I currently have the first volume of Heartstopper also out on library loan... I pray that her writing has improved or else I've made massive errors in thinking that she's a writer I could get on board with. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>For more reviews and book related chat check out <a href="https://alittlehazebookblog.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a></b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4262783107762805812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1819511888" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1819511888" />
    <a title="Ally" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15655618-ally"><img alt="Ally" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472122701p2/15655618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1819511888?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ally" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ally" href="/user/show/15655618-ally">Ally</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1819511888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4250479554482248658">Nope. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464371205ra/19233121.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I have a feeling I may just be way too worldly for this book. I mean, I'm old now. It's been a while since I was a teenager. But I guess my main beef with <i>Solitaire</i> is that, okay, sure its important for YA books to be relatable for the teenage audience it's aimed at, but that doesn't mean that it's okay for books to perpetuate harmful behaviours and attitudes and call it "brutally honest". <br/><br/>I know Alice Oseman was only what, seventeen when she wrote this. And, honestly? That's great. Howeve</span>
  <span id="freeText4250479554482248658" style="display:none">Nope. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464371205ra/19233121.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have a feeling I may just be way too worldly for this book. I mean, I'm old now. It's been a while since I was a teenager. But I guess my main beef with <i>Solitaire</i> is that, okay, sure its important for YA books to be relatable for the teenage audience it's aimed at, but that doesn't mean that it's okay for books to perpetuate harmful behaviours and attitudes and call it "brutally honest". <br><br>I know Alice Oseman was only what, seventeen when she wrote this. And, honestly? That's great. However... (and this is a potentially offensive however, so soz in advance) I don't always think being a writer and being a teenager go together. Throw rocks at me if you like, but its my opinion. I feel like, if you have a story to share, whatever age, that's truly awesome. But I feel like a story like <i>Solitaire</i> really needs some distance, some years and some perspective before it's put to paper. I'm not explaining this very well because I really don't want to offend all the teen writers out there, but writing benefits from life experience. <br><br>Like, take a look at Tori. She's apparently got a mental health problem which, from my experience, both personal and professional, is a difficult one to call. I heard recently that mental health problems amongst teenagers is at an all time high. One newspaper article went so far as to call it an epidemic. But when you examine what's going on, it's a lot more hazy than that. We've got anxiety, which so many people say they have. The vast majority of people I've spoken to who say they have an anxiety disorder also say they are self-diagnosed. Look, guys, <i>stop</i> self-diagnosing. If you genuinely feel like you have a problem, <i>go to your doctor</i>. Or another professional who is qualified in assessment. You cannot self-diagnose because, in all honesty, it makes the problem worse. You either end up sitting on the issue and not getting the help you need, or you have diagnosed yourself incorrectly and labelled yourself either wrongly, or unnecessarily. <br><br>A fuck ton of the anxiety that people feel is normal. Its <i>normal</i> to feel anxious in certain settings, at certain times of your life, in specific situations. <i>Everyone</i> gets anxious. It becomes a disorder that requires treatment when it prevents you from living your life. Its also normal to feel depressed sometimes. <i>No-one</i> has a steady mood, or a positive mood <i>all</i> the time. It's perfectly okay to feel off some days, or to feel down about things. Especially when you're a teenager. There's so much change that takes place during your teens years and its a tough time. You're growing and changing like, every day and it can be scary and overwhelming. I'm in no way trivialising anyone's experiences or feelings, but its perfectly sane and normal to be anxious or depressed during this time. Again, it becomes a problem that requires treatment when you can't function daily because of it. <br><br>Also what's important is that there is a <i>massive</i> difference between circumstantial and clinical mental health problems. Circumstantial means that like, you're down about life because everything is changing, or you feel like you're growing apart from people, or you're scared or overwhelmed about your future because you have so many decisions to make. Clinical is like, everything is great but you still feel like shit. Does that make sense? If you have a circumstantial problem, there's a ton you can do about it without labelling yourself with a mental health problem. Practise some self-care, go for a walk outside and get some fresh air, talk to someone about what's going on to make you feel this way (and be honest), take a look at your diet and sleeping pattern. It's not a good idea to leap to the conclusion that just because you're having a tough time, means you have a mental health problem. Trust me, you don't want that label. It follows you for a long time and can make the situation so much worse. I'm not saying that anyone who feels crap doesn't have a problem. Just that there are different "treatments" for different issues, and its super important to get to the actual bottom of the situation rather than labelling yourself with anxiety or depression and calling it a day.<br><br>That's the issue I have with books like this. They don't encourage a positive outlook on mental health. They make it seem like its okay to behave in a perpetually negative cycle. Tori is so unlikeable, it's unreal. She's rude, she's spoiled, she's selfish, she's judgemental. But yeah, because she's supposed to be suffering this undiagnosed and unspecified mental health problem, it's all fine!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467824788ra/19635247.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's not fine. <br><br><b>I don’t want people to be worried about me. There’s nothing to worry about. I don’t want people to try and understand why I’m the way I am, because I should be the first person to understand that. And I don’t understand yet. I don’t want people to interfere. I don’t want people in my head, picking out this and that, permanently picking up the broken pieces of me.</b><br><br>Oh what a shame that people give a fuck. Because of course no-one understands Tori. No-one else in the entire universe has ever been a teenager before. See, what bugs me with this is that if Tori <i>did</i> speak up she would discover that there <i>are</i> other people who have been through tough times who could support her and help her find ways to cope with how she's feeling. To create a character who insists on isolating herself and feeling so fucking sorry for herself throughout the whole book, right up until almost the last page, is not encouraging anyone who's reading it, and maybe feels the same way, to choose the right path. Maybe Tori's struggle <i>is</i> relatable, but that's not enough. The book lacks value because it doesn't offer any other way of looking at the world that might genuinely benefit readers. I think maybe this is what I was getting at about the whole teen authors thing. Sure, you might be able to write an awesome contemporary novel that other teens can connect with, but you need to also be about to write the characters in that novel out of the hole you've created for them. Otherwise we wind up with self-absorbed, narcissistic, unhealthy bullshit like <i>Solitaire.</i> <br><br>There's so much crap in this book: the dumb, hard-to-believe mystery about the secret society, the way that feminism, the LGBTQ community and diversity is badly represented, the way that parental figures are portrayed, the horrible, stilted dialogue, the <i>constant</i> pop culture references that age the book the instant it hits shelves, the lacklustre story arc, the pale characterisation, the confusing finale. <br><br>If you wanna read <i>good</i> contemporary, this ain't it. I do not recommend. Over and out. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4250479554482248658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1039113010" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1039113010" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8769426-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430689841p2/8769426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1039113010?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/8769426-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

          marked it as dnf


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062335685" href="/book/show/22588585-solitaire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=e-arc">e-arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1039113010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8928045879937788096"><b><a href='http://www.nosegraze.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nose Graze</a> — Book reviews & blogging tips</b><br/><br/><div>I stopped reading this book at 27%.</div><br/><br/> Let's talk about Solitaire <br/><br/>In the book, Solitaire is some kind of blog/prankster group. We learn pretty quickly that their blog URL is <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://solitaire.co.uk'>http://solitaire.co.uk</a> . My first thought (which continued to bug me throughout the book) was: <em>"There's no way this domain name would be available."</em> I'm pretty sure every non-obscure dictionary word is taken at this point (at least with the original and most common TLDs, like .com, .net,</span>
  <span id="freeText8928045879937788096" style="display:none"><b><a href="http://www.nosegraze.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Nose Graze</a> — Book reviews &amp; blogging tips</b><br /><br /><div>I stopped reading this book at 27%.</div><br /><br /> Let's talk about Solitaire <br /><br />In the book, Solitaire is some kind of blog/prankster group. We learn pretty quickly that their blog URL is <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://solitaire.co.uk">http://solitaire.co.uk</a> . My first thought (which continued to bug me throughout the book) was: <em>"There's no way this domain name would be available."</em> I'm pretty sure every non-obscure dictionary word is taken at this point (at least with the original and most common TLDs, like .com, .net, .co.uk). And solitaire.co.uk was in fact registered about five years ago.<br /><br />I know this is a STUPID ASS thing to be annoyed about, but I couldn't get it to stop nagging me. That kind of stuff bugs me... #nerd.<br /><br />But beyond that, Solitaire (the group) didn't excite me. I know I only read to 27%, which isn't that far, but they just seemed like a stupid group who thought highly of themselves. And to make things even worse, some of the "hacking" things they did just seemed too far-fetched. Solitaire has basically "hacked" the whole school. They do all these pranks by messing with the speakers, TVs, and computers. At one point in the book, they somehow lock Tori inside a room, take control of a computer, open up Microsoft Word, type a message, and manage to disable keyboard/mouse inputs (so Tori bashing the keyboard doesn't do anything). This was all done remotely.<br /><br />I thought this seemed VERY unlikely. Sure, it might be possible to hack in and remote desktop into a computer if you knew the exact one and were familiar with the system, but the circumstances just seemed too far-fetched. Especially when Tori tried bashing on the keyboard and got no response. So I decided to consult Coding God on this matter. I told him about the circumstances and mentioned it's a <strong>school</strong> (that's important). He says:<br /><br /><blockquote>[The hackers] would need to find an exploit [the system] is vulnerable to, even though it's not likely running any services. Most schools are running firewall/antivirus and aren't listening for incoming connections. It would be very difficult/improbable. Basically, if it was up to date on patches as well then no way. Unless those kids have zero day exploits that most experts are dying to find. :P <br /><cite>Coding God: software engineer with a degree in computer science</cite></blockquote><br /><br />I know this is a fiction book and it doesn't have to be accurate. But when I read a contemporary book, I don't like having improbably or even fantasy-like elements in there. I guess it's just hard for me because I am a tech nerd and I like the hacking I read in books to sound reasonable, or at least have the steps/actions explained. Fair enough that maybe they're explained later on and I just didn't get that far... but in the moment it did annoy me and made the book less enjoyable.<br /><br />Oh, then, at 24% a character got on the computer and <strong>opened up Internet Explorer</strong>. I mean, seriously? Internet Explorer? Kill me now. And if there are any readers out there who do use IE, please switch to Chrome or Firefox immediately. (I'm not kidding. IE sucks and is commonly known to be the worst browser out there. Do yourself a favour and switch.)<br /><br /> Tori is one bitter bitch <br /><br />This main character (Tori) was one of the most unlikeable characters I've read in a long time. She was bitter, bitchy, and pessimistic. It's like she didn't know how to smile or laugh, but she was an expert on being judgemental and looking down on people.<br /><br /> "Everyone else sucks! I'm the only real person in the world!" <br /><br />I think this might have been the most frustrating part of <em>
  <strong>Solitaire</strong>
</em> for me. Tori is bitter. She's pessimistic and judgemental. She doesn't seem to like people at all. She walks around with this "I'm better than you because I don't conform" attitude. I felt like she looked down on EVERYONE and it was exhausting.<br /><br /><blockquote>The large majority of teenagers who attend Higgs are soulless, conformist idiots. I have successfully integrated myself into a small group of girls who I consider to be "good people," but sometimes I still feel that I might be the only person with a consciousness, like a video game protagonist, and everyone else are computer-generated extras who have only a select few actions, such as "initiate meaningless conversation" and "hug."</blockquote><br /><br />She even kind of admits how bitter, pessimistic, and boring she is when she says this at one point:<br /><br /><blockquote>"Can you imagine me being excited about anything?"</blockquote><br /><br /> "My mom is so annoying so I'm going to be a bitch to her" <br /><br />Tori had such a weird relationship with her mom. I don't know if there was a bad history there or what, but she was kind of a bitch to her. I didn't think it was 'cool' or necessary. It just made her look even more annoying and bitchy.<br /><br /><blockquote>"Tori," says Mum, "Oliver should have been in bed an hour ago." <br />Oliver doesn't seem to hear her. I glance up from the race. <br />"That's not really my job," I say.</blockquote><br /><br /> "I like to snap at people for no reason" <br /><br />This character Lucas gets introduced and he and Tori used to be best friends. So he starts talking about how much she's changed since he last knew her, and she decides to be all snappy and bitchy to him, just because. In fact, she seems pretty snappy to him throughout the whole book (that I read). But poor Lucas was never anything but nice.<br /><br /><blockquote>"You're so different," he says [...]. "You're more serious." <br />[...] "I'm, well, I am probably the least funny person since Margaret Thatcher." <br />"No, but you were always dreaming up all these imaginary games. Like our Pokémon battles. Or the secret base you made out of the cornered-off section of the playground." <br />"Would you like to have a Pokémon battle?" I fold my arms. "Or am I too unimaginative for that?" <br /><em>"No."</em> He's digging himself into a hole, and it's actually quite funny to watch. "I—oh, I don't know."</blockquote><br /><br /> "Sometimes I do stupid, pointless things for no reason" <br /><br />At one point, Tori gets recruited to be part of kind of a campus lookout type programme. Solitaire is pranking the school and they want students to patrol the school and be on the lookout for them (break-ins, suspicious behaviour, etc.). So the leader gives Tori her number just in case she sees anything while on her watch and...<br /><br /><blockquote>"Here's my number." <br />I nod at her and go to walk off. <br />"Er, Tori?" <br />"Yeah?" <br />"You look a bit—" She doesn't finish her sentence. <br />It's 7:00 a.m. She can piss off. <br />I walk away, throwing the piece of paper in a bin as I pass it.</blockquote><br /><br />So she throws away the number immediately. Then when she DOES see something, she doesn't have the number to call the girl. Then she decides not to tell her anyway. Yeah, stupid.<br /><br /> "I hate books because they're boring" <br /><br />I think this was the final straw for me Tori-wise. She admits that she hates books.<br /><br /><blockquote>Coming out as a book hater to my dad is comparable to coming out as gay to homophobic parents.</blockquote><br /><br />It was at that point that I realized: I love books! Why should I waste my time reading about a bitter bitch who hates them?<br /><br /> Please, make it end! <br /><br />I spent like three days just getting to the 27% mark. Tori was incredibly unlikeable and there was nothing in the plot or other characters that hooked me in. I had no desire to keep reading and every desire to start <em>Take Me On</em> by Katie McGarry. So long, Solitaire.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8928045879937788096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3124177534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3124177534" />
    <a title="Zitong Ren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77983193-zitong-ren"><img alt="Zitong Ren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552188473p2/77983193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3124177534?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zitong Ren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zitong Ren" href="/user/show/77983193-zitong-ren">Zitong Ren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=contains-romance">contains-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=not-fantasy-2020">not-fantasy-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3124177534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3989670137260098029">From what I know, this is Alice Oseman’s Debut novel, and compared to her other books that I have read of hers, which are Radio Silence and I Was Born For This, this book does not live up to the quality of those two books. I was excited to start this one since I loved those two books and comparing these two to this book is that I can certainly say that she has improved greatly as a writer.<br/><br/>Now, I’m not one that reads many contemporary novels, and as such, I may be sprouting absolute rubbish in my</span>
  <span id="freeText3989670137260098029" style="display:none">From what I know, this is Alice Oseman’s Debut novel, and compared to her other books that I have read of hers, which are Radio Silence and I Was Born For This, this book does not live up to the quality of those two books. I was excited to start this one since I loved those two books and comparing these two to this book is that I can certainly say that she has improved greatly as a writer.<br /><br />Now, I’m not one that reads many contemporary novels, and as such, I may be sprouting absolute rubbish in my review, and for that, I apologise. I would simply like to start with the fact that the entire book was a bit weird and there’s no real plot or anything really as to what is actually going on, which left me a the reader not knowing what the entire objective of the book was. Many things also don’t make a whole lot of sense as to why such a thing happened, or even how, some of the events in this book occurred as the reasoning from some characters feel really poor. Almost as if the author didn’t know but needed it to work and was just like, here you go, I know this doesn’t make sense but deal with it.<br /><br />If I am being honest, the character development with the main character was very minimal, whenever there appeared to have some change occurring from her depressive state, she simply went back again, which I understand that the author is trying to show a character battling depression. The thing is, was that I would have liked to maybe see her slowly come out of it, or even to slowly accept for who she is, which would have been nice instead of from what we got.<br /><br />Now, like I mentioned above, the entire story really does not go anywhere, maybe except for the very end, despite how overly dramatic and perhaps slightly unrealistic it was. It just feels like a mindless collection of parties, going to school and all that, which, probably might have been fine if the reader was given some character progression, which didn’t really happen all that much. Everyone was where they had started from the beginning of the book, except for the last fifty odd pages. Leaving it to the end is great and all, but I normally need something else to compel me on instead of just a book that is essentially ‘day in the life.’<br /><br />Also, wow, they are lots of annoying characters that seem to be there for the sake of being annoying to show how bad the character’s state is in. Some of the actions from the characters honestly had me slightly perplexed though this may have been exemplified by the unreliable narration from a character that is ultimately depressed.<br /><br />While I have really enjoyed two other contemporaries by this author, this one ultimately fell a bit flat for me. 5.5/10</span>
  <a data-text-id="3989670137260098029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3262227380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3262227380" />
    <a title="Lucy Tonks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90494494-lucy-tonks"><img alt="Lucy Tonks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593371745p2/90494494.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3262227380?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Tonks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Tonks" href="/user/show/90494494-lucy-tonks">Lucy Tonks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007559220" href="/book/show/40683413-solitaire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90494494-lucy-tonks?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/90494494-lucy-tonks?shelf=2020-favourites">2020-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3262227380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9672970570251255644"><i>"All I know is that I’m here. And I’m alive. And I’m not alone."</i><br/><br/>This has just become one of my favourite books. I do think that I liked Radio Silence a little bit better, but man this is right next to it. I just loved this book so much. I was a little bit hesitant going into this book since I've seen a lot of people saying that this book is not as good as Alice Oseman's other works but I personally really loved it.<br/><br/>TW: suicide, self-harm, depression, eating disorders, obsessive-compulsive behavio</span>
  <span id="freeText9672970570251255644" style="display:none"><i>"All I know is that I’m here. And I’m alive. And I’m not alone."</i><br /><br />This has just become one of my favourite books. I do think that I liked Radio Silence a little bit better, but man this is right next to it. I just loved this book so much. I was a little bit hesitant going into this book since I've seen a lot of people saying that this book is not as good as Alice Oseman's other works but I personally really loved it.<br /><br />TW: suicide, self-harm, depression, eating disorders, obsessive-compulsive behaviours, incidents of homophobia (for more in depth trigger warnings check Alice Oseman's website) <br /><br />Random thought, but at the moment I'm not sure if I want a haircut like Tori's because of her or is quarantine simply getting to me (again. I already got side bangs and bleached half of my hair this year, I don't need another risky decision). <br /><br />The plot was so interesting and intrigued and I just loved following Tori along. To be honest, at the end I realised what was going to happen, but only because this was mentioned in Radio Silence. Through out the book I didn't make any connections with Radio Silence, but as I got to the end it clicked together. <br /><br />I really liked Tori as a character. I really connected with her and I also related with her, a lot.. I always end up relating with a character when it comes to Alice Oseman's books. For example in Radio Silence I found both Frances and Aled relatable and in Heartstopper I had a lot in common with Charlie. Basically I also find introverts relatable. But I simply found Tori's character extremely intriguing since she was different. She wasn't as other characters that I read about. I don't even know how to explain and I wouldn't because it would just come out wrong. <br /><br />I liked Michael and the relationship taht he established with Tori through out the book. Although there were times when I was frustrated by the way they were interacting with eachother, by the way they managed to screw thinsg up, I still really liked it but the end, I just wished we got more of it. <br /><br />This book was amazing and I loved it so much that I'll probably give in and read this novel again soon. This is not a book for everybody. Keep that in mind before picking this book up since this is a pretty dark book about mental health and sometimes it can get pretty graphic. <br /><br /><i>"I don’t want people to be worried about me. There’s nothing to worry about. I don’t want people to try and understand why I’m the way I am, because I should be the first person to understand that. And I don’t understand yet. I don’t want people to interfere. I don’t want people in my head, picking out this and that, permanently picking up the broken pieces of me."</i><br /><br />P.S. If anyone knows any books that are similar to this one or any other Alice Oseman books please hit me up, I really wanna read more books like this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9672970570251255644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_976485029" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/976485029" />
    <a title="Lauren ✨ (TheBookishTwins) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12484813-lauren-thebookishtwins"><img alt="Lauren ✨ (TheBookishTwins) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566649689p2/12484813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/976485029?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren ✨ (TheBookishTwins) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren ✨ (TheBookishTwins) " href="/user/show/12484813-lauren-thebookishtwins">Lauren ✨ (TheBookishTwins) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12484813-lauren-thebookishtwins?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12484813-lauren-thebookishtwins?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12484813-lauren-thebookishtwins?shelf=fav-2014-reads">fav-2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12484813-lauren-thebookishtwins?shelf=highly-anticipated-2014">highly-anticipated-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12484813-lauren-thebookishtwins?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12484813-lauren-thebookishtwins?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer976485029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer466950711656780009"><i>"There comes a point, though, when you can't keep looking after other people anymore. You have to start looking after yourself."</i><br/><br/><i>Solitaire</i> is a refreshing and brutally honest realistic fiction written by a teenager (Alice Oseman is only nineteen) for teenagers so it's totally and utterly relatable. <br/><br/>You know what I loved the most about <i>Solitaire</i>? Tori. Whilst she's cynical, sarcastic and rather mentally troubled, she's <i>real</i> and it's great to read and see her develop and I loved every second of it.</span>
  <span id="freeText466950711656780009" style="display:none"><i>"There comes a point, though, when you can't keep looking after other people anymore. You have to start looking after yourself."</i><br /><br /><i>Solitaire</i> is a refreshing and brutally honest realistic fiction written by a teenager (Alice Oseman is only nineteen) for teenagers so it's totally and utterly relatable. <br /><br />You know what I loved the most about <i>Solitaire</i>? Tori. Whilst she's cynical, sarcastic and rather mentally troubled, she's <i>real</i> and it's great to read and see her develop and I loved every second of it. I also loved Michael Holden and his <s>bumpy</s> touching relationship with Tori and how, at the end, it was all about acceptance. <br /><br />The Solitaire aspect of the story invited mystery and suspense, and although I guessed early on who was behind it, the reveal is still rather spontaneous. <br /><br />For a debut novel, <i>Solitaire</i> was fantastic and I'm looking forward to reading more from Alice Oseman in the future.<br /><br />I would highly recommend to fans of contemporary realistic fiction, and fans of authors such as John Green.<br /><br /><b>A lot of thanks to Alice for sending me a free (signed &amp; annotated throughout - this made my reading experience <i>so</i> much better. I won in an instagram giveaway) copy to read!</b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="466950711656780009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1200955469" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1200955469" />
    <a title="Natalie (Never trust a duck)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12682794-natalie-never-trust-a-duck"><img alt="Natalie (Never trust a duck)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391720998p2/12682794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1200955469?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie (Never trust a duck)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie (Never trust a duck)" href="/user/show/12682794-natalie-never-trust-a-duck">Natalie (Never trust a duck)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062335685" href="/book/show/22588585-solitaire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12682794-natalie-never-trust-a-duck?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12682794-natalie-never-trust-a-duck?shelf=laugh-out-loud">laugh-out-loud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12682794-natalie-never-trust-a-duck?shelf=british-boyz">british-boyz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12682794-natalie-never-trust-a-duck?shelf=met-my-fictional-husband-s">met-my-fictional-husband-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12682794-natalie-never-trust-a-duck?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12682794-natalie-never-trust-a-duck?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12682794-natalie-never-trust-a-duck?shelf=bringing-out-the-sleuth-in-me">bringing-out-the-sleuth-in-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12682794-natalie-never-trust-a-duck?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1200955469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13405172885036706919"><i>Thank you Andye from <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.readingteen.net/'>http://www.readingteen.net/</a> for your Review my Books program!</i><br/><br/>I quite honestly really really really enjoyed this book. Honestly. Solitaire was a major win.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424393292ra/13755985.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Get it? XD<br/><br/>When the synopsis says it is "unflinchingly honest", it speaks the truth. Alice Oseman wrote a brilliant contemporary. Though I wouldn't expect anything else from a fellow 90s child. ;)<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409455307ra/10981718.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>This book is hard to explain. I went into it knowing merely what it has printed on the cover, "This is the story of...Tori. Michae</span>
  <span id="freeText13405172885036706919" style="display:none"><i>Thank you Andye from <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.readingteen.net/">http://www.readingteen.net/</a> for your Review my Books program!</i><br><br>I quite honestly really really really enjoyed this book. Honestly. Solitaire was a major win.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424393292ra/13755985.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Get it? XD<br><br>When the synopsis says it is "unflinchingly honest", it speaks the truth. Alice Oseman wrote a brilliant contemporary. Though I wouldn't expect anything else from a fellow 90s child. ;)<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409455307ra/10981718.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>This book is hard to explain. I went into it knowing merely what it has printed on the cover, "This is the story of...Tori. Michael. Becky. Lucas. Charlie. And the year that changed everything." Not much to go on really. But it takes place in Britain and has British boys and British diction so, happy times for us Americans.<br><br>Victoria Spring, Tori as she likes to be referred to, doesn't try. Nor does anyone else for that matter. Everyone just doesn't <i>care</i>, according to Tori, and so she doesn't either. That is, until Solitaire infiltrates her school and Michael Holden infiltrates her busy schedule of wallowing in self pity and pessimistic thoughts. But I like Tori. She may be a bit of a Debbie Downer and push everyone away with her "Don't try" attitude, but she grew on me. Because she started to try. Mostly thanks to her new-found maybe gay maybe straight friend, Michael Holden.<br><br>Michael Holden's characterization is the work of a genius. He is. Just. So. <i>FUN.</i> A freaking fantastic boy. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"He's a very ordinary-looking, not ugly but not hot, miscellaneous boy. His most noticeable feature is a pair of large thick-frames square glasses, the sort similar to those 3D cinema glasses that twelve-year-olds pop the lenses out of and wear because they think it makes them look "rad." God, I hate it when people wear glasses like that. He's tall and has a side part. In one hand he holds a mug; in the other, a piece of paper and his school planner."</i>
</blockquote> <br><br>So basically he's perfect. <br><br>This book was a mystery. Solitaire is this anonymous blog that starts arranging pranks around the school. All of them seem to relate to Tori for some reason. But why? THAT'S THE QUESTION. So yes, it requires you to put on your sleuthing cap.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424392391ra/13755913.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>It's not just a mystery though, it's about realizing you don't have to do everything alone. It's okay to open yourself up. It's just an overall brilliant book, so give it a go.<br><br>I'll give you one more look into why Michael is perfect. <br><br><blockquote>
<i>"They locked you in this room," he says, "and you still don't care. Why not consider it this way: They're the evil criminal organization and you're Sherlock Holmes. I'll be John Watson. But we've got to be the Benedict Cumberbatch and Martin Freeman Sherlock and Watson, because the BBC Sherlock is infinitely greater than all other adaptations."<br>I stare at him.<br>"It's the only adaptation that gets the bromance</i> right<i>."<br>"You're a</i> fangirl<i>," I whisper, with mock horror."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>He <i>understands us</i>.<br><br>Happy Reading!!!<br><br><i>All quotes were taken from an ARC</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13405172885036706919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3169934996" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3169934996" />
    <a title="Meags" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8542123-meags"><img alt="Meags" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524277146p2/8542123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3169934996?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meags" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meags" href="/user/show/8542123-meags">Meags</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007559220" href="/book/show/40683413-solitaire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=mf">mf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=disability-illness-mentalhealth">disability-illness-mentalhealth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=hurt-comfort">hurt-comfort</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=library-borrows">library-borrows</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3169934996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1462050733659961273"><b>4 Stars</b><br/><br/>Solitaire is a unique, thought-provoking, and immersive YA story – one that captures the genuine highs and lows of the high school experience and takes a deeper look at the affects that mental health problems (both acknowledged and unacknowledged) can have on teenagers, including issues relating to depression, anxiety and eating disorders.<br/><br/>Now, that all sounds a bit on the heavy side, but I promise it’s not all doom and gloom. In fact, even with the themes surrounding mental health, which </span>
  <span id="freeText1462050733659961273" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars</b><br /><br />Solitaire is a unique, thought-provoking, and immersive YA story – one that captures the genuine highs and lows of the high school experience and takes a deeper look at the affects that mental health problems (both acknowledged and unacknowledged) can have on teenagers, including issues relating to depression, anxiety and eating disorders.<br /><br />Now, that all sounds a bit on the heavy side, but I promise it’s not all doom and gloom. In fact, even with the themes surrounding mental health, which are taken seriously and are represented truthfully, the overall tone of this very British story remains fairly laid-back and, at times, witty and self-deprecating, featuring a relatable cast of teenage characters and a slight mystery plot that keeps the story moving at an engaging pace.<br /><br />For those playing at home, this doesn’t really have a romance element, as such, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[it's more pre-slash for the MCs <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but the characters and their relationships, new and old and ever-changing, were more than fascinating enough to keep this usual romance reader interested and entertained. <br /><br />Truthfully, I found this to be really easy reading, enjoying Oseman’s quirky and candid (but quality) writing style to be refreshing and completely appealing. I’ll definitely be reading more from this talented young author in the future.<br /><br /><br />NOTE: This debut novel, by the author and artist of the since-popular <a href="https://heartstoppercomic.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Heartstopper webcomic</a>/<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/236821-heartstopper" rel="nofollow noopener">graphic novel series</a>, is set almost two years after fan-favourites Charlie and Nick first met and fell in love. Here, they play secondary roles to main character Tori Spring, Charlie’s slightly older, moodier sister, but all Heartstopper fans should find great joy in reading more about these guys, now a few years into their relationship. But be warned: issues relating to Charlie’s mental health struggles, which have only just begun to unfold in the available Heartstopper volumes/chapters, are discussed in detail here and may technically be experienced as spoilers for readers who have solely read the comics and don’t particularly want to know what is to come for Charlie and Nick in future volumes/chapters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1462050733659961273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56766903-miriam?shelf=illness">illness</a>,
