        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2363107968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18230350081069526846">Just finished my first book for this week's Read-A-Thon with the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/556982-goodreads-inspired-read-a-thon?ref=nav_bar_discussions_pane_group' rel='nofollow noopener'>Goodreads Inspired Read-A-Thon</a> -group :) <br/>________________________<br/><b>3.5 stars!</b><br/><br/>I already read Alice Oseman's Radio Silence and really enjoyed it, so I decided to give her debut a try as well. I must admit that I liked Radio Silence more, but I take this as an evidence that she clearly has developed as an author. <br/><br/>What impresses me most about her books is clearly her writing style. I think she manages to capture a teenager's thoughts ver</span>
  <span id="freeText18230350081069526846" style="display:none">Just finished my first book for this week's Read-A-Thon with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/556982-goodreads-inspired-read-a-thon?ref=nav_bar_discussions_pane_group" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads Inspired Read-A-Thon</a> -group :) <br />________________________<br /><b>3.5 stars!</b><br /><br />I already read Alice Oseman's Radio Silence and really enjoyed it, so I decided to give her debut a try as well. I must admit that I liked Radio Silence more, but I take this as an evidence that she clearly has developed as an author. <br /><br />What impresses me most about her books is clearly her writing style. I think she manages to capture a teenager's thoughts very well and writes them down in a way that flows and makes it easy as a reader to get absorbed by the story. This kind of saved this book for me, because there was just not enough plot for my taste. It was fascinating to witness Tori's way of seeing life, but there never was real tension. I found it rather easy to deduce the mystery around Solitaire, so the ending didn't really keep me on the edge of my seat. <br />Normally I like character-driven stories and can easily forgive unperfect stories, but most of the characters remained kind of shallow. They were full of flaws in a way that made them totally predictable. <br /><br />In addition, the characters in this book had a really negative opinion towards school and education in general. I already noticed this in Radio Silence and it keeps nagging me. It's obvious that the average teenager doesn't enjoy going to school a lot, because it is stressful and you have to work a lot etc. I don't know if it is a cultural thing, but this one-sided view was hard to tolerate for me. We often tend to forget how grateful we should be for being given access to education. School is not perfect of course, neither is university, but the attitude promoted in this book is exaggeratd in my opinion. <br /><br />To summarize it, this is a solid read for all contemporary-lovers.<br /><br />I had a few i</span>
  <a data-text-id="18230350081069526846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6520030732690013921">4/4.5*<br/><br/>Alice Oseman even at the age of 17-19 when she wrote and published this, was/is such a gifted storyteller! This book and the characters aren't perfect, but that's what makes them real. Which if you've read this book you know, is something the main character Tori's finds out about the people in her own life.   <span id="freeText6520030732690013921" style="display:none">4/4.5*<br /><br />Alice Oseman even at the age of 17-19 when she wrote and published this, was/is such a gifted storyteller! This book and the characters aren't perfect, but that's what makes them real. Which if you've read this book you know, is something the main character Tori's finds out about the people in her own life. There are quite a few trigger warnings in this book, but in my own opinion, I think they were handled with care. I can't wait to read Alice's other later works, and see how she has developed as an author! <br />This book made me FEEL!!! Happiness, sorrow, frustration, love, and just about a million other emotions. That's why I read books, to simply feel.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1423071768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1423071768" />
    <a title="spencer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29377707-spencer"><img alt="spencer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605244321p2/29377707.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1423071768?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="spencer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="spencer" href="/user/show/29377707-spencer">spencer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062335685" href="/book/show/22588585-solitaire">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1423071768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14914067178205061972"><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“I don’t want people to be worried about me. There’s nothing to worry about. I don’t want people to try and understand why I’m the way I am, because I should be the first person to understand that. And I don’t understand yet. I don’t want people to interfere. I don’t want people in my head, picking out this and that, permanently picking up the broken pieces of me.” </i>
</b><br/><br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1403739806l/22588585.jpg' width='400' height='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>____________________________<br/><br/>Going into this book, I was very excited to read this. I love Marina and the Diamonds and this seem</span>
  <span id="freeText14914067178205061972" style="display:none"><br><br><b>
  <i>“I don’t want people to be worried about me. There’s nothing to worry about. I don’t want people to try and understand why I’m the way I am, because I should be the first person to understand that. And I don’t understand yet. I don’t want people to interfere. I don’t want people in my head, picking out this and that, permanently picking up the broken pieces of me.” </i>
</b><br><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1403739806l/22588585.jpg" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>____________________________<br><br>Going into this book, I was very excited to read this. I love Marina and the Diamonds and this seems unrelated to the whole point of the book, but give me a moment to explain. Marina has a song out called Solitaire and I <b>LOVE</b> it. So, I thought it would be like this. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445739047i/16697999.jpg" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And I know that might not make sense, but I expected the book to almost feel like how I felt while listening to the song. Because in the lyrics to the song Marina says "Don't wanna talk anymore. I'm obsessed with silence." and that's how the main character is. And this book had some interesting references to things like Harry Potter, Beyoncé, Coldplay, Jane Austen, The xx, Noah and the Whale, Fleet Foxes. I don't know what to say other than that I was disappointed, because this book would essentially be everything I could ask for out of a book but the whole book was very underwhelming. <br><br><b>
  <u>1) The Plot</u>
</b><br><br>To be honest I don't even know how to describe this book. It's very interesting, let me tell you. Okay, so our main character Tori is the socially awkward, apathetic, slightly depressed going into her final year at a new school. And eventually she follows a trail of post-it notes to a computer lab being renovated with the computer working and on the computer it says SOLITAIRE. And then it's almost like the group Solitaire knows everything about Tori and tries to make it peaceful for her. Then all sorts of things go down and she wants to know who started it.<br><br>So, yeah, it's a little weird. But hey! This could be up your alley, but it wasn't for me. Also, this book takes place in England so it was a lovely change from the typical America. <br><br><b>
  <u>2) The Characters</u>
</b><br><br><b>Tori</b>- I'm not sure how I feel about her. Because emotionally wise, I felt pretty connected to her but then I slowly disconnected.<br><br><b>Charlie &amp; Nick</b> - I did love Charlie because I felt connected to him because of eating disorders and suicide attempts and I just loved Nick as well because I love LGBT couples.<br><br><b>Becky</b> - I wasn't sure how I felt about her at first. But then at the end, she really proved herself to me.<br><br><b>Michael</b> - I really, really liked this guy. He's just so weird and I loved it.<br><br><b>Lucas</b> - I was not his biggest fan, but he was alright.<br><br><b>
  <u>3) The Writing</u>
</b><br><br>I will say her writing was very nice considering Alice Oseman, the author, wrote this book when she was 17.<br><br><i>-“You like to act as if you care about nothing and if you carry on like that then you’re going to drown in the abyss you have imagined for yourself.” </i><br><br><i>- “There’s a time and a place for being normal. For most people, normal is their default setting. But for some, like you and me, normal is something we have to bring out, like putting on a suit for a posh dinner.” </i><br><br><i>-“What can I say? People aren’t observant. People don’t question stuff like this. They never think twice about déjà vu when there could be a glitch in the Matrix. They walk past tramps in the streets without even glancing at their misfortune. They don’t psychoanalyze the creators of slasher-horrors when they’re probably all psychopaths.” </i><br><br><i>-"His smile, fleeting, fades. "I don't think anyone deserves disaster. I think a lot of people wish for disaster because it's the only thing left with the power to turn heads.""</i><br><br><b>
  <u>4) Overall Thoughts</u>
</b><br><br>I just thought it was okay, and I was very underwhelmed.<br><br><i>★★/5 stars!</i><br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14914067178205061972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1crh7L9spCX/Pj4kx/6LAM/ZDBjWZm/ptKTu/XDK2XJEHkOpQVd0GH0em356gmGYHnCmGt1M547/lRkP9d0Wcw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+SQJw+P87gEU+LgHcDCpjoJy0KaeJVGgOTI5n+VAgCVo8KuGHcc+PJbYHV3NTEMWU9t6pJUP2cdyA85tYFdPJA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15408378982854222262">Alice Oseman is an author/illustrator and was born in 1994 in Kent, England. She has written four YA contemporary novels about teenage disasters: SOLITAIRE, RADIO SILENCE, I WAS BORN FOR THIS, and LOVELESS. She is also the creator of LGBTQ+ YA romance webcomic HEARTSTOPPER, which is now published in physical form by Hachette Children's Books.<br/><br/>Alice’s first novel SOLITAIRE was published when she was</span>
  <span id="freeText15408378982854222262" style="display:none">Alice Oseman is an author/illustrator and was born in 1994 in Kent, England. She has written four YA contemporary novels about teenage disasters: SOLITAIRE, RADIO SILENCE, I WAS BORN FOR THIS, and LOVELESS. She is also the creator of LGBTQ+ YA romance webcomic HEARTSTOPPER, which is now published in physical form by Hachette Children's Books.<br /><br />Alice’s first novel SOLITAIRE was published when she was nineteen. Her YA novels have been nominated for the YA Book Prize, the Inky Awards, and the Goodreads Choice Award, and HEARTSTOPPER has been optioned for TV. She can usually be found staring aimlessly at computer screens, questioning the meaninglessness of existence, or doing anything and everything to avoid getting an office job.</span>
